URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS94339886	11590.34	species	Red-and-green Macaw	Ara chloropterus			3			Panama	PA	Darién	PA-5				Darien--Cerro Pirre Trail	L934379	H	7.8610011	-77.6678467	1999-02-19	06:00:00	Coverage: We awoke at about 6:00 and birded around camp before breakfast and reset the mist nets. That morning we caught a Violet-headed Hummingbird, Rufous-cheeked Hummingbird and Olive-striped Flycatcher with the same reaction from the others in our group as in the previous day. I have banded over 25,000 birds in my life and I never cease to marvel at what birds look like in the hand.  While handling the birds I missed the Tooth-billed Hummingbird the rest of our group saw at camp and that turned out to be the last opportunity I would have to see this specialty of the Cerro Pirre. By 9:00 we were headed back down the trail to Cana and birding was very productive. We arrived at Cana about 13:00 and after lunch birded around the compound, winding up the day around the airstrip while looking at several species of Macaws. That evening, after two days of mud, mildew and grime I enjoyed one of the best showers I ever experienced.----Other observers: Brian Daniels, Dave De Sante, Pete Ginsberg, Tom Wurster, Dean Vanier.		obs27049	Peter	Ginsburg	S6567279	eBird - Traveling  Count	EBIRD	600	5		6	1	G177318	1	0		
URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS94339717	11590.34	species	Red-and-green Macaw	Ara chloropterus			3			Panama	PA	Darién	PA-5				Darien--Cana Mine/Camp	L934097	H	7.8354931	-77.6156616	1999-02-20	06:00:00	Coverage: Up at 6:00 and birded the mine trail but by 8:30 it was raining again and we waited until 10:00 before it stopped.  For the rest of the day, without rain, we birded the compound and Boca de Cupe trail, until 17:30 finding a small ant swarm and many good-sized flocks.  Birding was excellent! Our last dinner in the Darien was, as usual, quite good and we all agreed this was the birding experience we would not soon forget. Even with the inconvenience and at time discomfort and seemingly endless rain, I think it is the best place I have ever birded! URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS94340151	11590.34	species	Red-and-green Macaw	Ara chloropterus			1			Panama	PA	Darién	PA-5				Darien--Cerro Pirre Trail	L934379	H	7.8610011	-77.6678467	1999-02-17	07:30:00	Coverage: The prolonged, and at times driving rain through the night added to our level of anxiety about hiking to the top of Cerro Pirre in the morning.  We arose at 6:00 about the same time it stopped raining.  After breakfast we were on the trial by 7:30.  We all thought it a bit odd that Carmen Martino would tell us all to take a walking stick but as we would soon discover it was the only way we would be able to keep our balance on the very slick muddy trail up the mountain. We stopped many times to bird the many flocks we encountered on the hike. At 13:00 it started raining again making conditions on the trail even worse. For some inexplicable reason I had sent my rain gear up with the pack animals and without it I got soaked. As it turned out everyone else with rain gear got just as wet as I did from the humidity and sweat trapped under their rain gear.  We arrived at camp at about 13:30 and after a quick lunch that awaited us we started birding up the ridge. Despite the continuing rain we found many good-sized flocks and the birding was excellent.  We birded until dark and returned to camp for dinner and a welcomed nights sleep in individual tents where it was relatively dry.  There was just no getting around the humidity that we would experience during our entire stay in the Darien----Other observers: Brian Daniels, Dave De Sante, Pete Ginsberg, Dean Vanier, Tom Wurster		obs27049	Peter	Ginsburg	S6567283	eBird - Traveling  Count	EBIRD	480	10		6	1	G177320	1	0

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS90050681	11590.34	species	Red-and-green Macaw	Ara chloropterus			2			Venezuela	VE	Zulia	VE-V				Municipio La Cañada de Urdaneta, Campo Boscan	L889293	P	10.355	-72.1608333	2010-04-18	07:40:00	José Gustavo León, his young son José and his wife Karla Pérez, John Kvarnbäck, Andreina Sojo, and I spent most of the day today at two adjacent ranches located about an hour southwest of Maracaibo.  We reached these sites from the main highway via a side road at km. 56.  The first site we visited was Hacienda La Modelo (HLM; 7:40 am - 12:00 pm), which had mostly open pastures with scattered large trees, but we concentrated our time at several marshy areas and especially in some taller forest, with a canopy of 20+ m in height, along a small river that apparently reaches the Sierra de Perijá.  Although this forest now appears as a riparian corridor that still continues to the mountains, it really represents the remnants of what was once continuous, lowland forest that occurred throughout this region.  After we spent an extended period of time in this forest looking for landbirds, we continued over to the adjacent Hacienda La Zuliana (HLZ; 12:05-3:25 pm), where we concentrated our time at a marsh with several large, diked ponds that had much emergent vegetation, in places with dense stands of cattail.  Although we concentrated here on waterbirds, there were also grassy pastures with scattered large trees and some moderately tall woodland that was much like what we encountered at Hacienda La Modelo.  It was in the savanna-like part of the ranch that we spent some time looking for landbirds, both in the scattered large trees and also in a small patch of forest at the edge of the ranch.  It was partly cloudy all day, with a mild (5-10 knot) breeze at times, high humidity, and temperatures probably increasing from the mid-70s to the mid-90s.  7:40 am - 3:25 pm.----Falco sparverius / columbarius - 1 (a small falcon seen only briefly as it flew off was either a Merlin (as John thought) or a kestrel (as I was leaning), but we saw no color or pattern on the bird);--Myiozetetes sp. - 4;----Hydrochaeris hydrochaeris - 1 (standing in the middle of the marsh at Hacienda La Zuliana);--Alouatta seniculus - 1+ (I saw one in the forest along the river at Hacienda La Modelo but there were presumably others).
